<div id="review_1228816862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1228816862" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1228816862?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5280986-guards-guards">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own-backlog">own-backlog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1228816862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1413136512906265266"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I've had numerous people tell me this is the Discworld book to start with, and now I know why. Easily my favorite so far. 4.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>My Discworld read continues, and finally I come to infamous Guards! Guards! I know there are fancy diagrams and details on all the different ways you can read Discworld, but I prefer publish order. I've enjoyed all of the Discworld books so far, albeit some more than others. I generally seem to enjoy the Rincewind books less than I </span>
  <span id="freeText1413136512906265266" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> I've had numerous people tell me this is the Discworld book to start with, and now I know why. Easily my favorite so far. 4.5 stars.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />My Discworld read continues, and finally I come to infamous Guards! Guards! I know there are fancy diagrams and details on all the different ways you can read Discworld, but I prefer publish order. I've enjoyed all of the Discworld books so far, albeit some more than others. I generally seem to enjoy the Rincewind books less than I have the rest.<br /><br />A popular consensuses among several of my friends who have been reading Discworld for years seems to be that the City Watch books are the best and I should have started with this book. I can see why now. I'm only one book in, but I suspect these may become my favorites as well.<br /><br />Like all the Discworld books I've read so far, this one was very quotable and had numerous laugh out loud moments. However something about this book elevated it above the previous seven for me. I'm not exactly sure what.<br /><br />I love that the guards hate to be guards, and prefer not to do their job if at all possible. All of the guards are pretty enjoyable, but I especially like Carrot. I'll be curious to see what sort of character development Mr. Pratchett has in store for him (if any). The contrast of the big hulking human raised among dwarves who is so naive as to the point of obliviousness is highly amusing. Especially the fact that he has to be told he's not a dwarf. I also love the hints as to his real identity that I suspect will never go anywhere, because he's perfectly content at being a guard.<br /><br />The other highlights for me were the Librarian and the Patrician. They both had some great parts. We've seen some of the librarian in the previous books, but this is the first real interaction I recall with the Patrician. He's largely been mentioned in name only thus far.<br /><br />The story of this one was really enjoyable as well. Some of the previous books were funny at times with memorable characters, but the story was slow or disjointed. I liked the investigation into the cult of idiots by a Captain who'd rather be drunk. There were some great surprises along the way.<br /><br />Overall this book is clever, funny, and just downright enjoyable. I'm looking forward not only to the next Discworld book, but I'm especially looking forward to the next City Watch book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1413136512906265266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5686439842755546608">(4.5 stars, really.)<br/><br/>Perfectly structured, from beginning to end. Mean without being nasty, funny without being stupid. Insightful without being preachy. Terry Pratchett has a gift for lovingly pointing out the stupidities of the human condition. <br/><br/>This particular one is quite delightful. It's got dragons, a man named Carrot, and a group of three men who make up the city law enforcement, inept and lovable guardians of the backwards and corrupted joyful logic of the city called Ankh-Morpork. <br/><br/>Let me </span>
  <span id="freeText5686439842755546608" style="display:none">(4.5 stars, really.)<br /><br />Perfectly structured, from beginning to end. Mean without being nasty, funny without being stupid. Insightful without being preachy. Terry Pratchett has a gift for lovingly pointing out the stupidities of the human condition. <br /><br />This particular one is quite delightful. It's got dragons, a man named Carrot, and a group of three men who make up the city law enforcement, inept and lovable guardians of the backwards and corrupted joyful logic of the city called Ankh-Morpork. <br /><br />Let me leave you with this passage from the beginning of the novel: 'The city wasa, wasa, wasa, wossname. Thing. <i>Woman</i>. That's what it was. Woman. Roaring, ancient, centuries old. Strung you along, let you fall in thingy, love, then kicked you inna, inna, thingy. Thingy, in your mouth. Tongue. Tonsils. <i>Teeth</i>. That's what it, she, did. She wasa . . . thing, you know, lady dog. Puppy. Hen. <i>Bitch</i>. And then you hated her and, and just when you thought you'd got her, it, out of your whatever, then she opened her great booming rotten heart to you, caught you off bal, bal, bal, thing. <i>Ance</i>. Yeah. Thassit. Never knew where where you stood. Lay. Only one thing you were sure of, you couldn't let her go. Because, because she was yours, all you had, even in her gutters . . .'<br /><br />Also, this: 'It's a metaphor of human bloody existence, a dragon. And if that wasn't bad enough, it's also a bloody great hot flying thing.'<br /><br />And this: 'People were stupid, sometimes. They thought the Library was a dangerous place because of all the magical books, which was true enough, but what made it really one of the most dangerous places there could ever be was the simple fact that it was a library.'</span>

<div id="review_1114922159" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1114922159" />
    <a title="Michael" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4086118-michael"><img alt="Michael" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567611029p2/4086118.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1114922159?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael" href="/user/show/4086118-michael">Michael</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Michael by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4086118-michael?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114922159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5655093289839101716">I delighted in another visit to Discworld as an escape into the satire and silliness. But I found I had to be in the right mood, so it took me a long time to finish the book in small doses, the safest way with a dangerous recreational drug.<br/><br/>Our hero, Captain Vimes of the Night Watch, has less and less to do in his service to the metropolis of Anakh-Morpork. The city bureaucracy has become so efficient that all criminal sectors have become sanctioned under a set of guilds, allowing for a stable cr</span>
  <span id="freeText5655093289839101716" style="display:none">I delighted in another visit to Discworld as an escape into the satire and silliness. But I found I had to be in the right mood, so it took me a long time to finish the book in small doses, the safest way with a dangerous recreational drug.<br /><br />Our hero, Captain Vimes of the Night Watch, has less and less to do in his service to the metropolis of Anakh-Morpork. The city bureaucracy has become so efficient that all criminal sectors have become sanctioned under a set of guilds, allowing for a stable crime rate and taxes for their nefarious operations. His new youthful constable, nicknamed Carrot, has to be restrained from arresting all forms of legal offenders, which is getting them in trouble with city administration. They become energized with purpose when they discover signs of a dragon toasting buildings and people in the night, but no one believes them at first. <br /><br />Behind the scenes, the head of a religious brotherhood (Unique and Supreme Lodge of the Elucidated Brethren of the Ebon Night) has discovered a book on conjuring dragons in the library. The godlike power of controlling the appearance of such a beast is irresistible. The idea is born for bringing back a more lucrative government in the form of a monarchy. Once the city is terrorized enough by the dragon, the hero who can claim to conquer it will be a shoo-in to get anointed as king. It turns out that the people are craving the pomp of royalty and are eager for such a change. It is up to the Night Watch to bumble their way into foiling this plot. They have some help from one Lady Ramkin, who conveys her knowledge of dragons from her hobby of raising dog-size versions of the beasts of legend as pets. <br /><br />Much mayhem and silliness ensues, with Pratchett torturing the English language every chance he gets. How low or high does your taste in humor go? For example, Lady Ramkin’s diction is aptly captured in this sample:<br /><i>When she spoke, every word was like a hearty slap on the back and clanged with the aristocratic self-assurance of the totally well-bred. The vowel sounds alone would have cut teak.</i><br /><br />Vimes wonders why one of his men resort to kicking subdued criminals when they are already down:<br /><i> “Safest way, sir,’” said Nobby.</i><br /><br />It is not beneath Pratchett to milk the smallest turn of phrase to make us smile:<br /><i>In Vime’s professional opinion the palace guard these days were only one step away from being the worst criminal scum the city had ever produced. A step further <u>down</u>. They’d have to <u>reform</u> a bit before they could even be considered for inclusion in the Ten Most Unwanted List.</i>.<br /><br />Our bold author shows no compunction over taking logic over a cliff:<br /><i>…by and large medical assistance was nonexistent and people had to die inefficiently, without the aid of doctors. It was generally believed that the existence of cures encouraged slackness and was in any case probably against Nature’s way.</i><br /><br />He is shameless in taking puns and wordplay beyond where even Monty Python would dare to tread. For example, here the Librarian, who has the form of a gibbon due some old misapplied magic, is searching for the missing book late at night:<br /><i>Creatures evolve to fill every niche in the environment, and some of those in the dusty immensity of L-space were best avoided. Several times he had to flatten himself against the shelves as a thesaurus thundered by. He waited patiently as a herd of Critters crawled past, grazing on the contents of choicer books and leaving behind them piles of slim volumes of literary criticism. </i><br /><br />With more than 40 books in this series, this seems a fair choice for someone like me just getting my feet wet with only two read up to this point. In the right mood for playful diversion the story can serve as a fair comic parable of political corruption, illustrating how one misdeed from the wrong motive can escalate out of control and how the use of terror to get a populace to support a more powerful government can backfire when the instrument employed can no longer be controlled. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5655093289839101716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1259301918" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Lindsay" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay"><img alt="Lindsay" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588746288p2/10326608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1259301918?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsay" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsay" href="/user/show/10326608-lindsay">Lindsay</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1259301918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4618294463759404470">Continuing the Pratchett reread with the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads' rel='nofollow noopener'>SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group, we move on to one of my favorite books in the whole series and the start of one of the best sub-series in the overall Discworld universe.<br/><br/>Sam Vimes is the drunkard Captain of the nearly defunct Night Watch, down to three individuals and one raw recruit at the start of this novel. When the first proper dragon seen in centuries appears in the city of Ankh-Morpork the men (and one ape volunteer) of the Watch are all that stands agai</span>
  <span id="freeText4618294463759404470" style="display:none">Continuing the Pratchett reread with the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/162270-specfic-buddy-reads" rel="nofollow noopener">SpecFic Buddy Reads</a> group, we move on to one of my favorite books in the whole series and the start of one of the best sub-series in the overall Discworld universe.<br /><br />Sam Vimes is the drunkard Captain of the nearly defunct Night Watch, down to three individuals and one raw recruit at the start of this novel. When the first proper dragon seen in centuries appears in the city of Ankh-Morpork the men (and one ape volunteer) of the Watch are all that stands against it, stubbornly trying to do their job despite being the city joke.<br /><br />Vimes is a wonderful character. Deeply flawed and cynical, but an idealist to the core. It's actually the conflict of his ideals with reality that has brought him to the sorry state he is in at the beginning of this. It takes almost nothing, a starry-eyed recruit and a worthy foe, and he bounces back with a vengeance. Add in a brilliantly realized and hilarious supporting cast and finally we have the greatness that the Discworld has promised. Still a little way to go in the female characterizations though, even though Lady Sybil Ramkin is brilliant here (sadly she's not so brilliant again until <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/63720.The_Fifth_Elephant__Discworld___24__City_Watch___5_" title="The Fifth Elephant (Discworld, #24; City Watch, #5) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fifth Elephant</a> and the subsequent books.<br /><br />This is also an excellent place to start with the Discworld books if anyone is looking for a way into this dauntingly huge series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4618294463759404470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10910935591200926085">Rating: 3* of five<br/><br/><b>The Book Description</b>: Here there be dragons . . . and the denizens of Ankh-Morpork wish one huge firebreather would return from whence it came. Long believed extinct, a superb specimen of draco nobilis ("noble dragon" for those who don't understand italics) has appeared in Discworld's greatest city. Not only does this unwelcome visitor have a nasty habit of charbroiling everything in its path, in rather short order it is crowned King (it is a noble dragon, after all . . .).<br/><br/>Mean</span>
  <span id="freeText10910935591200926085" style="display:none">Rating: 3* of five<br /><br /><b>The Book Description</b>: Here there be dragons . . . and the denizens of Ankh-Morpork wish one huge firebreather would return from whence it came. Long believed extinct, a superb specimen of draco nobilis ("noble dragon" for those who don't understand italics) has appeared in Discworld's greatest city. Not only does this unwelcome visitor have a nasty habit of charbroiling everything in its path, in rather short order it is crowned King (it is a noble dragon, after all . . .).<br /><br />Meanwhile, back at Unseen University, an ancient and long-forgotten volume--The Summoning of Dragons--is missing from the Library's shelves. To the rescue come Captain Vimes, Constable Carrot, and the rest of the Night Watch who, along with other brave citizens, risk everything, including a good roasting, to dethrone the flying monarch and restore order to Ankh-Morpork (before it's burned to a crisp). A rare tale, well done as only Terry Pratchett can.<br /><br /><b>My Review</b>: I just don't care.<br /><br />Mildly amusing most of the time, smile-inducingly punny some of the time, and just...well...so what? Trenchant satire? Not to me. More like amusing cocktail party chatter.<br /><br />This is it for me and Sir Terry. I've tried, and frankly at 53, I don't see the need for me to read stuff that's as bland as unsalted rice.</span>

<div id="review_919962256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5454475-toby?shelf=fantastical">fantastical</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer919962256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6874583577673415437">Brilliant! Brilliant! Brilliant!<br/><br/>The debut outing of Sam Vimes, Carrot Ironfoundersson, Fred Colon, Nobby Nobbs, Sybil Ramkin, Detritus and Cutmeownthroat Dibbler,and what a barnstorming adventure it is. At this stage The Watch are a down and out bunch of losers who prefer to hide in the dark than doing any policing, led by the now legendary Sam Vimes who you'll find face down in the gutter drinking his misery away. And there are plots afoot in the city of Ankh-Morpork, plots to overthrow the Pat</span>
  <span id="freeText6874583577673415437" style="display:none">Brilliant! Brilliant! Brilliant!<br /><br />The debut outing of Sam Vimes, Carrot Ironfoundersson, Fred Colon, Nobby Nobbs, Sybil Ramkin, Detritus and Cutmeownthroat Dibbler,and what a barnstorming adventure it is. At this stage The Watch are a down and out bunch of losers who prefer to hide in the dark than doing any policing, led by the now legendary Sam Vimes who you'll find face down in the gutter drinking his misery away. And there are plots afoot in the city of Ankh-Morpork, plots to overthrow the Patrician with the help of a magical dragon long thought to be extinct even on a planet that has so much magic it doesn't know what to do with it. And so the inevitable clash between good and evil is set on its course in Guards! Guards!<br /><br />This was the first Discworld book I ever owned. A well meaning relative bought me a copy for my 9th birthday, I didn't understand a word of it and gave up pretty quickly. I've since wondered exactly what his thought process was in buying me that book. It took another 6 or 7 years before I read another one and I don't think that even then I was ready for how brilliantly funny or intelligent the work of Terry Pratchett on top form could be.<br /><br />Vimes is a perfect adaptation of the drunken noir hero who finds the strength to drag himself up out of the hole he'd retreated to via facing certain death in the name of something unselfish, and Pratchett throws in plenty of detective tropes from Doyle right on through to the 80s. His merry band of men come fully formed, characters you can't help but love and what a whirlwind Lady Sybil is, much more than just an upper class caricature.<br /><br />More! More! More!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6874583577673415437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_460623616" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460623616" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460623616?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series-opener">series-opener</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=faves">faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=discworld">discworld</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=magic-fantasy">magic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=mystery-crime-police">mystery-crime-police</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460623616" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8292955441164067746">I've read Sir Terry Pratchett's entire <b>City Watch Series</b> and the related <b>Moist Von Lipvig / Modernization series</b> (books listed below, in order). The entire series gets 4.5 solid stars, and it all starts here, with this book, and these characters (especially Captain Vimes). Such fun! Danger, suspense, action, relationship, character-development, humor, punnery, and plenty of satire. Plus, a little romance and...here be dragons.<br/><br/><i>Guards Guards</i> is the first book in the Discworld sub-series, where we </span>
  <span id="freeText8292955441164067746" style="display:none">I've read Sir Terry Pratchett's entire <b>City Watch Series</b> and the related <b>Moist Von Lipvig / Modernization series</b> (books listed below, in order). The entire series gets 4.5 solid stars, and it all starts here, with this book, and these characters (especially Captain Vimes). Such fun! Danger, suspense, action, relationship, character-development, humor, punnery, and plenty of satire. Plus, a little romance and...here be dragons.<br><br><i>Guards Guards</i> is the first book in the Discworld sub-series, where we meet Sam Vimes, captain of the Night Watch. In this book, we see him progress from boozing loser to protector of the people, champion of the city, dragon-slayer (sorta) and overall bad-ass hero. Also, there is a little romance, as Vimes connects with Lady Sybil Ramkin, the reigning dragon expert. <br><br><b>Goodboy Bindle Featherstone (Errol)<br>heroic swamp dragon!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438111801i/15666303._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>(art by Paul Kidby)<br><br><b>I loved LOVED the scene when Vimes riffs Clint Eastwood's DIRTY HARRY:</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The mob was threatening to kill Lady Sybil Ramkin's sickly swamp dragons, which only grow to about 2 or 3 feet tall. Vimes saves the day, fully outfitted in in his "night watch" uniform (snicker). <blockquote><i>A streak of green fire blasted out of the back of the shed, passed a foot over the heads of the mob, and burned a charred rosette in the woodwork over the door. <br><br>Then came a voice that was a honeyed purr of sheer deadly menace. "This is Lord Mountjoy Quickfang Winterforth IV. The hottest dragon in the city. It could burn your head clean off." Captain Vimes limped forward from the shadows, a small and extremely frightened golden dragon was clamped firmly under one arm. His other hand held it by the tail. <br><br>The rioters watched it, hypnotized. "Now, I know what you're thinking," Vimes went on softly. "You're wondering, after all this excitement, has it got enough flame left? And you know, I ain't so sure meself." He leaned forward, sighting between the dragon's ears, and his voice buzzed like a knife blade. "What you've gotta ask yourself is, am I feeling lucky?"</i></blockquote> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Sigh. I will read anything Sam Vimes. I also adore Lord Vetinari, the super-savvy sovereign, Lance Constable Carrot Ironfoundersson, Sergeant Fred Colon, Corporal Nobby Nobbs — a fabulous cast of characters. Eventually, we get a diverse mix of humans and fantasy figures, like trolls, dwarves, werewolves, dragons, gnomes, zombies, etc. <br><br>Even though the books are set on a fictional planet, the setting is similar to Old London, back when guild houses were prevalent. Pratchett and his faithful readers have made famous the fantastical planet Discworld and the vast twin-city of Ankh-Morpork. The city is ruled by The Patrician, a self-proclaimed tyrant, a dictator from the Assassin's Guild who goes by the title of Lord Vetinari. Love him. Didn't I say? ;)<br><br>Similar to old London, Ankh-Morpork is a city on the brink of advance. In fact, this is the city before an organized, equipped, and fully authorized <b>police system </b> even existed. Only the "Watch" existed, a handful of barely acknowledged men -- yes, all men at first -- who walked the beat. Or shuffled. Snoozed. Boozed.<br><br>In <i>Guards Guards</i> we see a more disciplined -- and more respected -- police force begin to take shape. In the sequels (Night Watch, Men at Arms, etc.) the fledgling police becomes more established, as Sam Vimes allows women to join the force, as well as dwarfs, trolls, werewolves, vampires, etc. Eventually, they move up in the world, getting new digs at Pseudopolis Yard -- yup, much like Scotland Yard. <br><br>Across the City Watch series and the cross-over series with Moist Von Lipwig (listed below) Pratchett weaves a <b>theme of tolerance, </b>of accepting and even embracing different species and races. Sometimes Pratchett waxes long on making this point, but usually he toes the line nicely.<br><br><b>Quibbles and complaints:</b> Only a few minor flaws, in my view. I enjoy Pratchett's brand of satire, but sometimes the narrative gets a bit preachy and/or teachy. Also, sometimes there are so many puns and parodies that the plot becomes secondary, momentarily. Some allusions and references are unknown to me. These are all minor quibbles.<br><br><b>
  <u>The Series:</u>
</b> In reading order, books featuring Sam Vimes (CW = City Watch series)<p>Guards! Guards! - 1989 CW<br>Theatre of Cruelty - 1993, CW (4 pages, free, <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.lspace.org/books/toc/toc-english.html">http://www.lspace.org/books/toc/toc-e...</a>) <br>Men At Arms - 1993 CW<br>Feet of Clay - 1996 CW<br>Jingo - 1997. CW<br>The Fifth Elephant - 1999 CW<br>The Truth - 2000 (minor character)<br>Night Watch - 2002 CW<br>Monstrous Regiment - 2003 (minor character)<br>Thud! - 2005 CW (and children's book <i>Where's My Cow?)</i><br>Unseen Academicals - 2009 (minor character)<br>Snuff - 2011 CW<br>Raising Steam - 2013 (supporting character)<br></p><b>(City Watch book links at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/106221-discworld---ankh-morpork-city-watch">https://www.goodreads.com/series/1062...</a>)</b><br><br><b>Related "Modernization" (some say "Industrialization") books:</b> There are some spin-off books that cross-over with the "City Watch" sub-series. These books introduce some modernization to the twin cities of Ankh-Morpork. The books feature <b>con-man turned hero, Moist Von Lipvig, </b> and a few characters from the City Watch. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/64222.Going_Postal__Discworld___33__Moist_von_Lipwig___1_" title="Going Postal (Discworld, #33; Moist von Lipwig, #1) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Going Postal</a> describes the invention and proliferation of postage stamps (loved it) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/116296.Making_Money__Discworld___36_" title="Making Money (Discworld, #36) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Money</a>, depicts the creation of paper money to replace gold (also very good). Then there is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11275323.Raising_Steam__Discworld___40_" title="Raising Steam (Discworld, #40) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Raising Steam</a>, where Lord Vetinari makes Moist Von Lipvig ensure that the newly invented locomotive is profitable and safe for the City (this is the last book written for Discworld).<br><br>Also, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/567670.The_Truth__Discworld___25_" title="The Truth (Discworld, #25) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">The Truth</a> depicts the invention of a printing press and the subsequent introduction of widespread newspapers into society. Satire deals with the wholesale acceptance of lies when ink-validated. William de Worde (he-he) is the city's first investigative journalist, sleuthing out possible murder and a plot to overthrow Lord Vetinari. This book does not feature Moist Von Lipvig, but it has some City Watch characters. <br><br>Finally, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34510.Moving_Pictures__Discworld___10_" title="Moving Pictures (Discworld, #10) by Terry Pratchett" rel="nofollow noopener">Moving Pictures</a> introduces the film industry to the eager citizens of Ankh-Morpork. This book does not include Moist Von Lipvig. I didn't care as much for it, but it's brimming with satire and some scenes are great.<br><br><b>!!! This chart is great for finding your way around the sub-series within the multitude of Discworld novels:<br> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://i.kinja-img.com/gawker-media/image/upload/s--nZhqj1Uo--/c_fit,fl_progressive,q_80,w_636/695333150797533991.jpg">http://i.kinja-img.com/gawker-media/i...</a></b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="8292955441164067746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_989791115" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989791115" />
    <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas"><img alt="Kaethe Douglas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573927565p2/1072582.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/989791115?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaethe Douglas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaethe Douglas" href="/user/show/1072582-kaethe-douglas">Kaethe Douglas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/5280986-guards-guards">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=watch">watch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=libraries">libraries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=swashbuckling">swashbuckling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1072582-kaethe-douglas?shelf=noir">noir</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer989791115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17116926591653123129">2009 January 1<br/>2014 August 16<br/><br/>In his first Watch book Pratchett introduces the old school noir police officer. Sam Vimes most notable characteristic at the outset is how much he drinks, and how the opened bottles are always present in his desk drawer, but he never remembers buying them. There is a dame, of course, but she's notable not for her looks, but for her good works. Sybil breeds the little dragons that people keep as pets for lighting fires.<br/><br/>The Night Watch is a minimal force: Vimes, Colon,</span>
  <span id="freeText17116926591653123129" style="display:none">2009 January 1<br />2014 August 16<br /><br />In his first Watch book Pratchett introduces the old school noir police officer. Sam Vimes most notable characteristic at the outset is how much he drinks, and how the opened bottles are always present in his desk drawer, but he never remembers buying them. There is a dame, of course, but she's notable not for her looks, but for her good works. Sybil breeds the little dragons that people keep as pets for lighting fires.<br /><br />The Night Watch is a minimal force: Vimes, Colon, Nobbs, and the new volunteer from the dwarves, Carrot. They aren't particularly competent, but no one expects them to do anything except walk the streets each night, saying "all's well" on the hour.<br /><br />Interesting note: Carrot memorizes the lawbook of Anhk-Morpork, many of the laws within date to the 1500 and 1600s. Not a lot of "century of the fruitbat" stuff here. This is a medievilish fantasy setting: the weapons are halberds, pikes, morningstars, bows. By the end Pratchett has brought the Watch into more-or-less modern policing.<br /><br />I'm having an insanely good time reading through the Discworld in arcs, rather than the more random order I read them in first. Now that I know all the characters it is much more fun to go back and see how the Watch as an institution and as characters have evolved. I'm still laughing at all the jokes I got the first time, but I'm also enjoying the grand changes over time. The early books were mostly about a bunch of guys, and then there are a few female characters, and then there are characters who aren't human, and the ecosystem keeps revealing more and more the closer one looks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17116926591653123129" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2651904615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3373842339270103391"><b>5 Words: law-and-order, responsibility, social-standing, power, dragons.</b><br/><br/>This was an excellent audiobook - I think that Nigel Planer did a great job narrating the story.<br/><br/>I love the humour in these stories, and I'm quite glad of my decision to tackle the Watch Novels first in my great Discworld reading challenge, as it's off to an excellent (and Rincewind free) start.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+R/rtHPHElLY//MbUywEqtBfEnVOh45ZM+UXrp2y7VvDOYJmyJnbOn/UR3qk2Q51BgD1vYAKAD5om1EfUPEfwQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('88Jvv4agH3psbagbSyOHEIlIWODv/c0Bia/vspjcFlDJ5AZtPf7WEstGHHq81o3PXxe/KCFwQ2bS0akDVZ/kyg==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p3/1654.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">Terry Pratchett

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6896878187591696532">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br/><br/>Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, i</span>
  <span id="freeText6896878187591696532" style="display:none">Born Terence David John Pratchett, Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <i>The Carpet People</i>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <i>The Color of Magic</i>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <i>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</i>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <i>Good Omens</i>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <i>Nation</i>. Terry published <i>Snuff</i> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire (OBE) “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from the University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, the University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6896878187591696532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
